  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6e133020-3994-418f-86b8-70e8ce4c805c'

<span id="freeTextContainer7501443720908441800">From National Book Award-winning, <em>New York Times</em>-bestselling author Louise Erdrich, a profound and enchanting new novel: a richly imagined world “where butchers sing like angels.”<br/><br/>Having survived World War I, Fidelis Waldvogel returns to his quiet German village and marries the pregnant widow of his best friend, killed in action. With a suitcase full of sausages and a maste</span>
  <span id="freeText7501443720908441800" style="display:none">From National Book Award-winning, <em>New York Times</em>-bestselling author Louise Erdrich, a profound and enchanting new novel: a richly imagined world “where butchers sing like angels.”<br /><br />Having survived World War I, Fidelis Waldvogel returns to his quiet German village and marries the pregnant widow of his best friend, killed in action. With a suitcase full of sausages and a master butcher's precious knife set, Fidelis sets out for America. In Argus, North Dakota, he builds a business, a home for his family—which includes Eva and four sons—and a singing club consisting of the best voices in town. When the Old World meets the New—in the person of Delphine Watzka—the great adventure of Fidelis's life begins. Delphine meets Eva and is enchanted. She meets Fidelis, and the ground trembles. These momentous encounters will determine the course of Delphine's life, and the trajectory of this brilliant novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7501443720908441800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1272622-just-finished-this-book-and-as-much-as-i"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Just finished this book and as much as I loved it I was left with many loose ends! We find out at the end that Delphine's father knew what he was doing with the family in his cellar. What I'm wondering about is what did Clarisse have (if anything) to do with all of this. The Sheriff was obsessed with her and that red dress with the sequins. He knew that he had something on her so she killed him and left. Why? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4199757-lynette-roberts">Lynette Roberts</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Clarisse didn't have anything to do with those in the cellar. Sheriff ripped her dress, that night, which is how the bead got there. Sheriff used this<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Clarisse didn't have anything to do with those in the cellar. Sheriff ripped her dress, that night, which is how the bead got there. Sheriff used this "evidence" for further contact with her.<br />What isn't clear is why she and Delphine acted so guilty.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_100645738" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100645738" />
    <a title="Barbara H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1883816-barbara-h"><img alt="Barbara H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572546566p2/1883816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100645738?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara H" href="/user/show/1883816-barbara-h">Barbara H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780066209777" href="/book/show/790393.The_Master_Butchers_Singing_Club">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Maria</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1883816-barbara-h?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1883816-barbara-h?shelf=ww-1">ww-1</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100645738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10182478952743778805">How does one review a book written by a true artistic voice and do justice to its telling? One should not expect a synopsis here, that can easily be found elsewhere. This is a beautiful, often painful novel.<br/><br/>Although Louise Erdrich generally places emphasis on the Native American in her books, she has chosen to take a different route with this novel. The occasional references to American Indians are by no means insignificant, however, but add spice to an already intriguing narrative. Her many, va</span>
  <span id="freeText10182478952743778805" style="display:none">How does one review a book written by a true artistic voice and do justice to its telling? One should not expect a synopsis here, that can easily be found elsewhere. This is a beautiful, often painful novel.<br /><br />Although Louise Erdrich generally places emphasis on the Native American in her books, she has chosen to take a different route with this novel. The occasional references to American Indians are by no means insignificant, however, but add spice to an already intriguing narrative. Her many, varied characters have come alive on the pages to give the reader a sense of recognition throughout. It is not difficult to develop feelings for these individuals, each with his or her intriguing situation. Erdrich has plumbed the depths and peaks of the emotions of her characters with stark, lyrical realism. Her narrative of the environment which existed for them was beautifully and palpably etched throughout.<br /><br />It is rare that I give a book a five star rating, but this seems to easily merit this place. Although I feel that much more can and should be said about this writer and her offering, I will continue to contemplate the messages that she has set down in her skillful writing.<br /><br /><br />NOTE: This review will be continued!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10182478952743778805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81558828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81558828" />
    <a title="Anika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/227324-anika"><img alt="Anika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202514459p2/227324.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81558828?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anika" href="/user/show/227324-anika">Anika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780066209777" href="/book/show/790393.The_Master_Butchers_Singing_Club">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/227324-anika?shelf=gah-frustrating">gah-frustrating</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer81558828&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81558828" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8424941196486690187">This book was incredibly frustrating. Erdrich has plenty of skill setting up the beginning of a story - she does it about twelve times - but never manages to actually stay with any particular arc. Stories and characters are established just enough to whet your interest, and then she just wanders to another one. Think you'll be staying with Fidelis, the titular master butcher, after he travels from Germany to North Dakota? Meh, he'll sort of be around, but you'll never get a better sense of how h</span>
  <span id="freeText8424941196486690187" style="display:none">This book was incredibly frustrating. Erdrich has plenty of skill setting up the beginning of a story - she does it about twelve times - but never manages to actually stay with any particular arc. Stories and characters are established just enough to whet your interest, and then she just wanders to another one. Think you'll be staying with Fidelis, the titular master butcher, after he travels from Germany to North Dakota? Meh, he'll sort of be around, but you'll never get a better sense of how he ticks. Want to know what the clear and immediate attraction between him and Delphine will lead to? That story will totally peter out and happen pretty much offstage. Interested in the murder mystery that gets set up, or the story of Delphine's friend? None of these things will ever really be focused on. You end up with a serious case of literary blue balls, wishing that the author had been as interested in her own characters as you are. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8424941196486690187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1941553968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1941553968" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1941553968?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780060531973" href="/book/show/7116503-the-master-butchers-singing-club">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-history">american-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family-sagas">family-sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=literary-novel">literary-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-novel">american-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=drama">drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1941553968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6780792808092107518">Louise Erdrich's literary novels are filled with rainbows of different time periods in history, and include expanded lists of characters which could focus on different events and personalities and paints a colorful portrait of life, even if the hues are dark and uncompromising. I guess her books are like certain gourmet foods. An acquired taste. <br/><br/>If I can compare it with other books similar in ambiance, authors such as Amy Tan, Lisa See, Wiley Cash, Erskine Caldwell, Cormack McCarthy and Jonis Ag</span>
  <span id="freeText6780792808092107518" style="display:none">Louise Erdrich's literary novels are filled with rainbows of different time periods in history, and include expanded lists of characters which could focus on different events and personalities and paints a colorful portrait of life, even if the hues are dark and uncompromising. I guess her books are like certain gourmet foods. An acquired taste. <br /><br />If I can compare it with other books similar in ambiance, authors such as Amy Tan, Lisa See, Wiley Cash, Erskine Caldwell, Cormack McCarthy and Jonis Agee comes to mind.<br /><br />I enjoyed this novel set in North Dakota beginning after WWI and ending after WWII. German immigrants settled down in a small town where Fidelis Waldvogel and his wife Eva opened up a butchery and try to fit into a new society. <br /><br />Their paths crossed with local characters with which they form strong bonds, when Fidelis started the master butcher's singing club. <br /><br />It became the story of women enduring tough challenges while being involved in different forms of relationships with men and among themselves. <br /><br />It's not a book for the fainthearted since many brutalities adorn the plot and were often revolting. However, the prose is beautiful in all its blasé-glory. There's no other way of describing the captivating experience, although it took some guts at times to continue reading. <br /><br /><i>The Round House</i> was my first encounter with this author's work. The writing style is unique, authentic, grounded, honest and real. <br /><br />Well, this is North Dakota-noir, intense, Gothic and dark at times, but an unforgettable good reading experience. Masterfully written. In an inexplicable way I felt immensely enriched.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6780792808092107518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_615826746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615826746" />
    <a title="Elaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2352900-elaine"><img alt="Elaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505699475p2/2352900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615826746?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/2352900-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2352900-elaine?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615826746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11891536020620262099">This is a lumpy weird passionate sweep of a novel. There was lots that irked me - pacing that speeded up and then slowed way way down and the central passion seems hollow (and mostly happens offstage) - but I read compulsively nonetheless. <br/><br/>Indeed, the book's real passions are the all the non-couple pairings- women friends, parents and children, adoptive parents, platonic male and female pairs - and these relationships are intense and compelling and give the book a wonderfully rich texture. It's </span>
  <span id="freeText11891536020620262099" style="display:none">This is a lumpy weird passionate sweep of a novel. There was lots that irked me - pacing that speeded up and then slowed way way down and the central passion seems hollow (and mostly happens offstage) - but I read compulsively nonetheless. <br /><br />Indeed, the book's real passions are the all the non-couple pairings- women friends, parents and children, adoptive parents, platonic male and female pairs - and these relationships are intense and compelling and give the book a wonderfully rich texture. It's just that we are supposed to believe that the earth moved when our hero and heroine so much as glanced at each other. And that rang false. <br /><br />But it ultimately doesn't matter because there's so much strange meaty life here. The book is full of imagery about things that worm their way up out of cellars and soil, that won't stay buried, and the narrative is similarly constructed - a North Dakota town in the middle of nowhere ends up being the knot where many threads of history and mystery come together. The Native American genocide, World War I, the Holocaust - it's all there, or you can just read this book as a quirky gothic family tale. Unlike the recent Erdrich (The Round House) I read, this book is not didactic. The Master Butchers Singing Club's slaughters - of Native Americans, livestock, wild dogs - are gutpunchingly stark and brutal (an awful lot of dead things in this book), but the tone is never hectoring. <br /><br />Ultimately, the book sprawls over its margins a bit. A lot is started, and like life, only some of it is finished. But the gritty, bloody, earthy vibrancy is very compelling and I forgave the book its lumpiness. <br /><br />I will say that this book is not for the squeamish. There were several extended sequences where I felt literally nauseous reading - I quickly learned this was not a breakfast table book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11891536020620262099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_186965478" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186965478" />
    <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw"><img alt="Doug Bradshaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548429066p2/808994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186965478?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug Bradshaw" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw">Doug Bradshaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186965478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13151829735386701213">Louise Erdrich is the Master writer story-teller. For me, one of the marks of a great writer is their ability to explain and make us feel human emotion and psychology that is subtle and virtually unexplainable. This book is chuck full of such amazing and spot on observations about how people think and why they do what they do to each other. <br/><br/>The story covers the period from the end of WW1 through and beyond WW2 and is about a simple German fellow and his bride who move to the US for a better life</span>
  <span id="freeText13151829735386701213" style="display:none">Louise Erdrich is the Master writer story-teller. For me, one of the marks of a great writer is their ability to explain and make us feel human emotion and psychology that is subtle and virtually unexplainable. This book is chuck full of such amazing and spot on observations about how people think and why they do what they do to each other. <br /><br />The story covers the period from the end of WW1 through and beyond WW2 and is about a simple German fellow and his bride who move to the US for a better life and end up settling in a small town in North Dakota and then eke out an existence as a butcher with meat market. At the same time, a local girl with a tough background living without a mother and only an alcoholic father, also eking out an existence with her boyfriend doing balancing acts and shows in nearby towns, meets the Germans and an interesting partnership is born. <br /><br />Here are some additional random thoughts about the book and contain ***SPOILERS***:<br /><br />1. The book is very graphic about the world of slaughtering animals, the smells, the cleaning rituals, the ruined hands, the bones molding in the back yard, dogs taking away carcasses and on and on. She must have grown up on a farm and must have experienced first hand the elements of raising animals. There wasn't much left to the imagination. She tells the whole story and I was there experiencing it all with the family.<br /><br />2. Although the two wars and violence of both wars and the suffering and the odd position American Germans were in is written about, the historical aspect and history of the wars is a minor detail and not the main story. The main story is the interaction over the years between an amazing and lovable female character and the German couple and their four children, most of it set in their meat market. <br /><br />3. The main female character is young and naive and has had a difficult life growing up. Although the words homosexual or gay were not use then, her handsome and talented boyfriend turns out to be gay. She actually discovers this by observing him having sex with another man in a hidden wooden area. She was far enough hidden and away that she couldn't see the details of what was happening, but it was an excellent and heartbreaking sub-story that seemed so very real that I had to wonder if the author went through something similar. I had to keep thinking to myself that this author, who is three years younger than me and published the book 8 years ago, has been through a lot and has seen a lot and hasn't had a particularly easy life either.<br /><br />4. There were some minor disappointments. Since her gay boyfriend was such a disappoint to her sexually, I was hoping we'd get to hear that her relationship with the man who became her husband was stellar. But there was never any mention of it. That brings up another of the author's excellent writing skills. Many of the relationships between male and females in the book are paced so carefully and occur with only minor incremental growth and progress that it was somewhat hard on me. I wanted closure now, things to be easier and fixed like I hoped they eventually would be. But it ended up that when I finally got what I hoped was coming, it was more rewarding than it would have been.<br /><br />5. There is gruesome death here, genealogy that will floor you in the very last chapter, a little fun PG13 sex, death caused by war, extreme and realistic love and caring. <br /><br />I didn't love the title of the book, but I did enjoy all of the comments about the singing club. Give this one a try. It is truly outstanding.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13151829735386701213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18500410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18500410" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/998334-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205944593p2/998334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18500410?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/998334-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people i purposely enjoyed frustrating</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18500410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6263785940693397728">VERY mixed feelings about this book. The author has some beautifully worded sentences and an overall engaging story (in the sense that it would have made a good screenplay) however, what the author states in the included interview as to her intention for writing the book (1--to show the affects of war and 2--to show the difficulties of immigrants to build a life in a country devoid of familial support or the familiarity of cultural fortification)was at best, used as a backdrop for a story about </span>
  <span id="freeText6263785940693397728" style="display:none">VERY mixed feelings about this book. The author has some beautifully worded sentences and an overall engaging story (in the sense that it would have made a good screenplay) however, what the author states in the included interview as to her intention for writing the book (1--to show the affects of war and 2--to show the difficulties of immigrants to build a life in a country devoid of familial support or the familiarity of cultural fortification)was at best, used as a backdrop for a story about the friendship of two women. Even the title is misleading as the importance of the club is not even effectively woven throughout the story, but disappears and then pops up at odd intervals. The same could be said of the character from whose perspective the story is initially told; he seems to be only a vehicle for introducing us to the two women upon whom the majority of the novel is focused.<br /><br />I finished the book thinking that the author's intentions were very poorly implemented and that I felt shorted by the fact the novel left me with no entertaining questions or themes other than wondering why it deserved to be published. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6263785940693397728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1383810615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383810615" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1383810615?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=university-library">university-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383810615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8663346926049819441">Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>When I first started reading <i>The Master Butchers Singing Club</i>, my initial response was “Not another war book!” as I am not a fan of war fiction. Both World Wars do feature in the book, but they do not overpower the story, for which I am very thankful.<br/><br/>I don’t think that I have ever before consciously encountered a book set in the period between the two World Wars and that is odd—it’s a very rich period of history to explore. The author’s style reminded me strongly of Canad</span>
  <span id="freeText8663346926049819441" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br /><br />When I first started reading <i>The Master Butchers Singing Club</i>, my initial response was “Not another war book!” as I am not a fan of war fiction. Both World Wars do feature in the book, but they do not overpower the story, for which I am very thankful.<br /><br />I don’t think that I have ever before consciously encountered a book set in the period between the two World Wars and that is odd—it’s a very rich period of history to explore. The author’s style reminded me strongly of Canadian author Robertson Davies (a compliment coming from me, as I adore his Deptford series, which also deals with small town characters). Her characters are very unique and yet they are ordinary people, living ordinary lives in many ways. Alcoholics, orphans, poor people, butchers, singers, Native people, circus people, murderers, undertakers, pilots, children, all making their way through the world as best they can. Erdrich doesn’t make them flamboyantly odd, just the regular peculiar that one finds in small communities. It strikes me that this could have been a Canadian book—the northern U.S. shares many environmental and cultural threads with Canada, I think.<br /><br />This is probably also the best depiction of a love triangle that I have ever encountered in literature. Several triangle relationships hinge on Fidelis, the master butcher. His wife Eva and her friend Delphine. His sister Tante and Delphine. Fidelis, Delphine and Cyprian. And yet, as his name would indicate, Fidelis is faithful to each of the women in his life. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He is the provider for Eva until her death, considers Tante until she returns to Germany, and waits until he is sure that Cyprian is truly gone before proposing to Delphine. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Another pseudo-Canadian theme in the novel is that of identity, a well-worn Canuck obsession. We get to watch Delphine struggle with her lack of knowledge about her origins, and see each of Fidelis’ sons forge lives for themselves and decide where their hearts lie.<br /><br />So many underlying themes, well written, and thought provoking. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8663346926049819441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1101428284114289368">******************************************<br/><br/>Louise Erdrich likes to sneak up behind us and surprise us with what we already know but are trying to forget.<br/><br/>Death and life are the same. Our own lives lead us towards our own deaths as we live from the proteins that we harvest from those other living creatures killed for our nourishment. And we, ourselves, live and die for the nourishment of others.<br/><br/>That which we see around us is so much more than we suspect; but is hidden from us by, not only our own s</span>
  <span id="freeText1101428284114289368" style="display:none">******************************************<br /><br />Louise Erdrich likes to sneak up behind us and surprise us with what we already know but are trying to forget.<br /><br />Death and life are the same. Our own lives lead us towards our own deaths as we live from the proteins that we harvest from those other living creatures killed for our nourishment. And we, ourselves, live and die for the nourishment of others.<br /><br />That which we see around us is so much more than we suspect; but is hidden from us by, not only our own self-imposed illusions, but also by the deceptions imposed upon us by others for our own, and their own, protection.<br /><br />This book plays out those realities in ways that confuse and deceive us so that we may then learn for ourselves that which we have forgotten.<br /><br />This is one more gem; and Louise Erdrich keeps making jewelery.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2831384952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2831384952" />
    <a title="Joy D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50297885-joy-d"><img alt="Joy D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450639623p2/50297885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2831384952?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy D" href="/user/show/50297885-joy-d">Joy D</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060935337" href="/book/show/1088891.The_Master_Butchers_Singing_Club">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=migration">migration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=north-america">north-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=native-american">native-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=family-dynamics">family-dynamics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=zck">zck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2831384952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9375442020100189717">Fidelis, a former WWI German sniper, marries Eva, his deceased friend’s pregnant fiancé, and emigrates from Germany to Argus, North Dakota, to establish a butcher’s shop. Delphine, daughter of an alcoholic single father, meets Cyprian, a former WWI US Marine, and they create a traveling acrobatic act. They eventually return to Argus and pretend to be married to avoid gossip. Delphine and Eva become fast friends, and the storyline follows their converging lives from WWI to several years past WWII</span>
  <span id="freeText9375442020100189717" style="display:none">Fidelis, a former WWI German sniper, marries Eva, his deceased friend’s pregnant fiancé, and emigrates from Germany to Argus, North Dakota, to establish a butcher’s shop. Delphine, daughter of an alcoholic single father, meets Cyprian, a former WWI US Marine, and they create a traveling acrobatic act. They eventually return to Argus and pretend to be married to avoid gossip. Delphine and Eva become fast friends, and the storyline follows their converging lives from WWI to several years past WWII. <br /><br />The strengths of this novel include deeply drawn characters and an unusual plotline. The characters are complex, filled with internal contradictions. For example, Fidelis is a butcher so he seems rather unfeeling in his work of constantly killing animals, but he possesses a beautiful singing voice and treats his family with tenderness. Even the minor characters exhibit a unique identity and emotional depth. <br /><br />War and its ongoing impact are recurrent themes. Initially, war affects Cyprian and Fidelis, but the next war wreaks havoc on Fidelis’s sons. The plot includes such diverse elements as the discovery of three bodies in a cellar, a sexual identity crisis, and a tie-in with the Wounded Knee massacre. There are a few brutal scenes, mostly involving animals. Several mysteries get set up and are not always resolved. It is rich in period details and beautifully written. By the end, the author has taken the reader in unexpected directions and several secrets are revealed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9375442020100189717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_793937305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793937305" />
    <a title="Stephanie Sun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118030-stephanie-sun"><img alt="Stephanie Sun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589823798p2/118030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793937305?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Sun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Sun" href="/user/show/118030-stephanie-sun">Stephanie Sun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780066209777" href="/book/show/790393.The_Master_Butchers_Singing_Club">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118030-stephanie-sun?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118030-stephanie-sun?shelf=alternating-close-3rd-person">alternating-close-3rd-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118030-stephanie-sun?shelf=george-w-bush">george-w-bush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118030-stephanie-sun?shelf=bechdel-test">bechdel-test</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793937305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9851324247527385912">Sort of a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7354.The_Shipping_News' title='The Shipping News by Annie Proulx' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shipping News</a> meets <b>Fargo</b>, set in the 1920s, 30s, and 40s. The characterizations are uneven and spazzy; the narrative unaccountably choppy; but Erdrich does captivate and compel here and there.<br/><br/>The best part is the amazing descriptions of food:<br/><br/><i>"...breakfast of cheese and bread and <b>stewed prunes</b>... ...coriander, pepper, and apple-wood-smoked pork, a rich odor, clean and bloody and delicious... ....every mood of red—twenty or thirty cuts of meat, summer sausage, <b>liver sausage</b>, beer sa</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9851324247527385912" style="display:none">Sort of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7354.The_Shipping_News" title="The Shipping News by Annie Proulx" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shipping News</a> meets <b>Fargo</b>, set in the 1920s, 30s, and 40s. The characterizations are uneven and spazzy; the narrative unaccountably choppy; but Erdrich does captivate and compel here and there.<br /><br />The best part is the amazing descriptions of food:<br /><br /><i>"...breakfast of cheese and bread and <b>stewed prunes</b>... ...coriander, pepper, and apple-wood-smoked pork, a rich odor, clean and bloody and delicious... ....every mood of red—twenty or thirty cuts of meat, summer sausage, <b>liver sausage</b>, beer sausage, veal, blood, Swedish, Italian and smoked pepper sausage, glistening hearts and liver and pale calf thymus, <b>sweetbreads</b>, as well as a great box of the delicately spiced, unsmoked, boiled wieners... ...Try this <b>lard</b>. For fish, it is good. Pure as butter!... ...fresh coffee and a <b>cinnamon bun</b> exquisistely dotted with raisins and sugar and butter... ...Old World Quality sausages prepared with the simplicity and perfection common in the German street... ...Marzipan. Herring. <b>Pickles</b> with the right degree of spice. Rolls as soft... ...a jar of <b>dark, cold, homemade beer</b>... ...strong black Turkish coffee... ...cold butter cut into flour for a pastry: pies for the Fourth of July supper to cut the booze... ...a crock of <b>beans</b> laced with <b>hot mustard</b>, brown sugar and <b>black-strap molasses</b>... ...A bowl of <b>oatmeal</b> steaming hot, butter melting in a pool with a lump or two of dark brown sugar. Cream. Sometimes eggs or toast... ...a Hungarian-style <b>goulash</b>, a thick stew of braised meat in paprika sauce, ladled over spaetzle. Sour cream topping it... ...a stack of <b>pancakes</b> studded with the last of the sweet wild blue <b>saskatoons</b>. Dabbed butter on the top. Drizzled on a little maple syrup... ...<b>lemon pound cake</b>... ...fish in bacon grease... ...a <b>baked potato</b>, bacon drippings spooned into the soft meal... ...a plate of beans baked in tomato sauce, a large beer sausage, and half a sweet onion... ...<b>kidney gravy and mashed potato pie</b>... ...creamy <b>oyster soup</b> in a shallow bowl, crackers stuck all the way around it, peppered, a lump of butter on top... ...Traumfeuer on a hard piece of sweet bread and a bit of cream... ...dumpling soup... ...chocolate so dark it is almost black, that tastes of oranges... ...light <b>cheese</b> spread on toasted rolls in the morning, and jams of all kinds. Marmalade... ...sugar cookies in the shapes of animals, fried doughnuts, sausages, bread, hard cheese, apples, and bottles of beer... ...creamed chicken, creamed corn and spinach, mashed potatoes with butter and cream, pies and cookies set out on doilies cut of white paper... ...<b>Country bread</b> thickly spread with real sweet butter, ham perfectly smoked, cured, and cut fresh in a generous slab... ...sauerbraten everywhere we go, or forest venison..."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9851324247527385912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9329618281614296570">I love Louise Erdrich. Love her.<br/><br/>She is such a nuanced, intelligent, talented writer.<br/><br/>I would read anything she writes. I'd read her shopping list.<br/><br/>Even her weaker novels -- and there have been one or two -- are worth the read, simply for her lyricism and the way she elevates the act of storytelling into an art form.<br/><br/>The Master Butchers Singing Club is, I'm happy to say, one of her best. <br/><br/>Highly recommended.<br/><br/></span>

<div id="review_924676411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/924676411" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14773738-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509454384p2/14773738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/924676411?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/14773738-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer924676411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer691888899157953154">This was an oddly disturbing and challenging novel for me to get through, and yet, in the end I felt amply rewarded for my perseverance. I can't say that Erdrich has an easy style -- in fact, at times it is frustratingly obtuse, perhaps even deliberately so, but she still leaves a very tantalizing trail of breadcrumbs that you can't help put pick up after.<br/><br/>Throughout, we explore the weight of history: deeply personal stories of scarred individuals who --much like the rest of us -- struggle to mak</span>
  <span id="freeText691888899157953154" style="display:none">This was an oddly disturbing and challenging novel for me to get through, and yet, in the end I felt amply rewarded for my perseverance. I can't say that Erdrich has an easy style -- in fact, at times it is frustratingly obtuse, perhaps even deliberately so, but she still leaves a very tantalizing trail of breadcrumbs that you can't help put pick up after.<br /><br />Throughout, we explore the weight of history: deeply personal stories of scarred individuals who --much like the rest of us -- struggle to make sense of the progress of their lives, while dragging along the weight of their ancestors. Nicely confined within the ramparts of World Wars I and II, we garner a unique perspective on this era through Erdrich's deformed characters: some in body, others in soul. Unrelentingly, she exposes the tender cuts, and the raw wounds of the butchery of life: a master craftswoman in her own right.<br /><br />Be warned: it's work, and no mistake that you'll be exhausted by it. I'm not one, like so many others, who found it easy, or gripping from the start. For me, it worked its way under my skin slowly until I came to the realization that I would not soon forget these people because they'd attached themselves to my nerve-endings. The memory of this book will always be raw.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="691888899157953154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_199175212" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199175212" />
    <a title="Deb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5276322-deb"><img alt="Deb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526245087p2/5276322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199175212?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/5276322-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/16096302-the-master-butchers-singing-club">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199175212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4434484999667190504">This book was a complete and welcome surprise. Wonderful writing and an easy stream of words pull and guide you through this life cycle of a story <i>
  <b>The Master Butchers Singing Club.</b>
</i><br/><br/>I always seem to detail the shelf life or position of said book as it makes itself known to me. How I became familiar with it. It’s purchase. How long it sat on my hallowed shelves. How it made it to a final cut but then due to lack of ripeness ended up right back in its home snuggled in comfortably with other book</span>
  <span id="freeText4434484999667190504" style="display:none">This book was a complete and welcome surprise. Wonderful writing and an easy stream of words pull and guide you through this life cycle of a story <i>
  <b>The Master Butchers Singing Club.</b>
</i><br /><br />I always seem to detail the shelf life or position of said book as it makes itself known to me. How I became familiar with it. It’s purchase. How long it sat on my hallowed shelves. How it made it to a final cut but then due to lack of ripeness ended up right back in its home snuggled in comfortably with other books hoping to audition again soon for the pleasure of my company. This book is no different. It appeared at the audition several times only to be sent back again and again. Oh but the <i>
  <b>Master Butchers Singing Club</b>
</i>knew it’s worth and did not give up for a whole year, I think and thankfully I allowed it a chance to “show me what cha’ got”. <br /><br />What I got, was nothing like what I assumed this book to be. This was actually sort of a family/small town saga reminiscent of <i>Fall On Your Knees by Ann-Marie MacDonald</i> or <i>Songs in Ordinary Time by Mary McGarry Morris</i>. I’m actually shocked that Oprah hasn’t gotten her hands on this one yet. (In a good way.)<br /><br />We meet Fidelis Waldvogel as he collapses in exasperation across his bed in his childhood home in Germany after walking home from the devastation that he survived in World War I. Fidelis, exudes a measure of quiet strength of which benefits carried him safely through the war. Fidelis is a man of extreme honor. After bringing the bad news to his brother in arms fiance’, Eva, he offers himself in marriage and surrenders himself helplessly to an enduring dedicated love. This is the journey of Fidelis Waldvogel, a master butcher taught by his father, who immigrates to American with a suitcase full of expertly made German sausages, sharp knives and a dream. However, the life of this book is complete and this tale would be incomplete if there were not various characters to enhance, dance and live alongside the large presence that is Fidelis in the small town of Argus, North Dakota. Roy Watzka is the town drunk with a secret past. Delphine Watzka is Roy’s daughter who in the future lives a full and complex life but upon introduction is having a complicated relationship with closeted Cyprian Lazzare. Children grow. Seasons change. Residents live and die. The world turns and Step and a half walks the town with her cart full of rags and what not. Ups and downs. Curves and sharp turns. Anticipation, aggravation, justification.. So is <i>The Master Butcher’s Singing Club.</i> <br /><br />This book has so much, it is hard to be vague and give a review. But believe me, there is <b>so</b> much one could never give away all the nuances and complexities of this book. This was not a difficult read in the least and I enjoyed reading it. It is pretty darn close to a perfect score but falls short for just a few reasons. I make reference to the “life” in this book because it is full of the labyrinth of complexities that surround the various lives. There were various low points and climactic points but always just falling slightly short of “the big one”. Sorrow, but could have been deeper. Good but not perfect, just kinda ok. Possible brimming passion but no.. no, just smoldering. The possibility of tremendous “Wow” climatic points were set up and then.. no, no the characters ultimately are unfulfilled so reader you must also be (in keeping with the concept)… un-full-filled. Yes, Yes, Yes… Noooo. It was a lot without still being enough. Short. Like $.99 cents… enough.. but with one more penny it could be $1.00 a dollar. Just NOT enough. Like a hand full of cereal. It could tied you over but why not give milk, a spoon and a bowl for a meal.. Just NOT enough. Like fun without the happy ending. JUST not enough. I could go on, I won’t. ;o)<br /><br />Giving it a technical 4 ½ on the Deb score board. On the GR board it’s a 4 stars but know that silently.. (whispers) I give it that half!<br />Yes I recommend: historical fiction readers, international readers, Readers. It’s good. Good first start to my year of book challenge. <br /><br /><b>*******SPOILER DISCUSSION/OBSERVATION POINTS BELOW IF YOU DON’T WANT TO KNOW, DON’T SCROLL*********</b><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />-Interesting the relationship between Cyprian &amp; Delphine. He needed her and loved her as a sister but because he could not make the romantic sexual connection with the relationship this was just not enough for Delphine. I was glad when she turned down his proposal. To marry him would have been to steal all prospects of true intimacy. <br /><br />-I was disappointed for all Fidelis &amp; Delphine’s smoldering… it was all smoke with no fire!<br /><br />-Eva, the ultimate mother was a mother to all. Delphine, due to lack of mothering allowed Eva and Cyprian to mother her. <br /><br />-I ALWAYS knew Step and a Half was supposed to be her mother but not that she was still adopted. <br /><br />-The relationships with the grown up sons I felt could have been more in depth. <br /><br />-I don't know that the title fits because the club is not the focus.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4434484999667190504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1451024256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451024256" />
    <a title="Marc Gerstein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15102294-marc-gerstein"><img alt="Marc Gerstein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389185056p2/15102294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1451024256?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc Gerstein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc Gerstein" href="/user/show/15102294-marc-gerstein">Marc Gerstein</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15102294-marc-gerstein?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1451024256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5584470260729169467">The is an OK book that fell far short of what it could have been, the reason, probably, having to do with the authors revelation in the Acknowledgements that follow the text, specifically, the third and final paragraph in which she acknowledges that members of her family inspired key characters (although I suspect she give short shrift to the existent that Delphine is based on her grandmother).<br/><br/>This is a big, sprawling family saga with intriguing ethnic and historical angles. Normally I love work</span>
  <span id="freeText5584470260729169467" style="display:none">The is an OK book that fell far short of what it could have been, the reason, probably, having to do with the authors revelation in the Acknowledgements that follow the text, specifically, the third and final paragraph in which she acknowledges that members of her family inspired key characters (although I suspect she give short shrift to the existent that Delphine is based on her grandmother).<br /><br />This is a big, sprawling family saga with intriguing ethnic and historical angles. Normally I love works like this. And normally, I’m flabbergasted, in a good way, by the sort of linguistic craftsmanship Erdrich can obviously bring to the table, and often does in this work. Ultimately, though, I think she was way too close to her characters and stories and did not pull them off as effectively as she might have had she been able to approach them as a novelist. Fascinating story lines get set up, and then seem to dissipate, or vanish. Characters suddenly make bold leaps that leave the reader wondering how they got from there to here; after a while, I stopped backtracking to look for things I might have missed. And the pacing here was odd, verbal flourishes and rich detailed narration is wonderful -- in the right places. But Erdrich goes into it almost randomly and sometimes, it seems to take forever to traverse events not significant enough to warrant the Henry James treatment. And I really wish Erdrich would have been able to find a more artistically satisfying way of delivering the information we get in the final chapter which, as it stands, comes off as a clumsy add-on.<br /><br />I started with the intent of giving this three stars but I find that the more I write, the more likely I am to talk my rating down. I don’t want to go there since there is a lot here that was enjoyable and engaging; a terrific cast of characters for one thing and some wonderfully offbeat story lines. I’ll just stop here, with the three stars, and wish Erdrich had been able to detach her novelist self from her family memories and make this all it could have been.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5584470260729169467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37819791?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37819791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3264499108786891547">I hated to see this one end as I fell in love with the characters. In the first chapters you follow Fidelis Waldvogel from the World War I German battlefields, to his journey to America with only a suitcase of sausages and his master butcher knives. He lands in Argus, North Dakota, works for a time for Pete Kozka, always letting him know his intention to strike out on his own. This he does and the ensuing rivalry between the two is a story in itself. Enter two more well fleshed characters, Delph</span>
  <span id="freeText3264499108786891547" style="display:none">I hated to see this one end as I fell in love with the characters. In the first chapters you follow Fidelis Waldvogel from the World War I German battlefields, to his journey to America with only a suitcase of sausages and his master butcher knives. He lands in Argus, North Dakota, works for a time for Pete Kozka, always letting him know his intention to strike out on his own. This he does and the ensuing rivalry between the two is a story in itself. Enter two more well fleshed characters, Delphine Watzka , with the rock hard flat stomach that is used as a table by her friend and odd lover, Cyprian, a balancing expert with a traveling act. Add Ron , Delphine's hard drinking, poor excuse of a father with his own dark secrets, Step-and-a-half, the local rag picker, love, friendship, murder, and small town life as our nation recovers from one war only to lead into another, making this a story that is hard to put down. Erdrich blends her love of history and Ojibwa heritage yet again, in this saga. A bit long, perhaps, maybe too much story for one book, but still, the characters absolutely shine. A good choice for book groups. I haven't read an Erdrich book in a long time and was quite entertained by this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3264499108786891547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1168230531" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1168230531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17273465595105142577">Story set in the years between the end of The Great War and WWII. Fidelis Waldvolgel returns from the war to deliver the news of his best friend, Johannes's death to a young and very pregnant Eva. Fidelis vowed to marry Eva in Johannes' stead and Eva, in her grief, accepts. The story then follows Fidelis, now a master butcher like his father, as he travels to America and takes the train west as far as his money will take him which ends up being Argus North Dakota. Fidelis begins working for a bu</span>
  <span id="freeText17273465595105142577" style="display:none">Story set in the years between the end of The Great War and WWII. Fidelis Waldvolgel returns from the war to deliver the news of his best friend, Johannes's death to a young and very pregnant Eva. Fidelis vowed to marry Eva in Johannes' stead and Eva, in her grief, accepts. The story then follows Fidelis, now a master butcher like his father, as he travels to America and takes the train west as far as his money will take him which ends up being Argus North Dakota. Fidelis begins working for a butcher who has already set up shop, and he eventually earns enough to bring Eva and baby Franz to join him. They have another baby, Markus, and then twins boys, Erich and Emil. They purchase an old homestead at the edge of town, and open their own butcher shop.<br /><br />About the time that the new shop is becoming successful, a prodigal child returns to Argus. Delphine Watzka, daughter of the town drunk, returns from her travels as a performer in a side-show balancing act with her "husband", Cyprian. The relationship between Delphine and Cyprian is not what it seems but they love each other, in a way, and support each other through many difficult times. Delphine's story is complicated, and she turns to Eva as a sort of surrogate mother, as her how own mother died long ago, when Delphine was a toddler. Eva takes to Delphine and they soon become the best of friends. Years go by, many things happen, clear up to the end of WWII.<br /><br />The first half of the book was very good, but it seemed like the author lost steam when it came to recounting life after the boys grew up. The reveal about Delphine's mother was so odd coming at the very end like that. I thought it could have come sooner and been explored a bit more but that's not what happened. I think this could have been much better but it wasn't bad either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17273465595105142577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_42342504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42342504" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/330370-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188590074p2/330370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42342504?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/330370-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/330370-mara?shelf=american-indians">american-indians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/330370-mara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/330370-mara?shelf=wwi">wwi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/330370-mara?shelf=germany">germany</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/330370-mara?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/330370-mara?shelf=immigrants">immigrants</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42342504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3635658549617444699">	The master butcher's singing club of the title doesn't really figure into this book at all. Fidelis, the master butcher in question, does start a singing group in his new home of Argus, North Dakota, that's meant to reflect the master butcher's singing club he was a part of back in Germany, as a place where outside grievances can be set aside.<br/><br/>But this story is really about Delphine, a native of, though an outsider in, Argus. It's about her relationship with men, sort of, but really about what s</span>
  <span id="freeText3635658549617444699" style="display:none">	The master butcher's singing club of the title doesn't really figure into this book at all. Fidelis, the master butcher in question, does start a singing group in his new home of Argus, North Dakota, that's meant to reflect the master butcher's singing club he was a part of back in Germany, as a place where outside grievances can be set aside.<br /><br />But this story is really about Delphine, a native of, though an outsider in, Argus. It's about her relationship with men, sort of, but really about what she discovers when she meets Eva, Fidelis's wife. In Eva, Delphine discovers the mother she never had, as well as a best friend. That Delphine comes to love Eva's family as her own is fortunate when Eva is struck with a massive tumor. Delphine nurses her until her death and then cares for Fidelis and their sons.<br /><br />All of this makes for a story that is lovingly told. What threw me for a loop, though, was at the very end of the book when the truth about Delphine's mother is revealed to the reader, but not to Delphine herself. Although I was vaguely interested to have this mystery cleared up, I don't really think it was necessary to the story at all. By including it at the end, it seemed as though we were supposed to think that this revelation was the whole point of the story, rather than an incidental part of the character Delphine became. The answer provided excellent closure to the story as a whole, but part of me wishes Erdrich had finished the book without it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3635658549617444699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
